## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics – nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard state-space form of an oscillator ODE. Nonlinear harmonic oscillator models typically combine a restoring force depending on x, damping depending on v, and possibly time-periodic forcing/parametric excitation depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (state form): dv_dt = -c0 * x (ideal spring-mass restoring acceleration)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**3 (nonlinear stiffness plus linear damping)
- Quintic stiffness nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 (stronger amplitude-dependent restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag-like): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (damping magnitude grows with speed)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (velocity-opposing friction with nearly constant magnitude)
- Pendulum small-to-large angle restoring: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (bounded restoring force from geometry)
- Conservative oscillator from potential U(x): dv_dt = -(c0 * dU_dx) with dU_dx = c1 * x + c2 * x**3 (force as negative gradient of potential)
- Externally forced oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (time-periodic drive)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**3 + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear stiffness under periodic forcing)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness)
- Van der Pol type self-oscillation (negative linear damping at small amplitude): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (limit-cycle generating damping nonlinearity)
- Rayleigh type self-oscillation (nonlinear damping in v): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (limit-cycle via velocity-dependent damping)
- Polynomial-in-state surrogate (common in symbolic regression of oscillators): dv_dt = c0 + c1 * x + c2 * v + c3 * x**3 + c4 * x**2 * v + c5 * x * v**2 (generic truncated normal form near an equilibrium)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces typically give dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -x**3, -sin(c*x)); even powers of x often indicate broken symmetry or bias.
- Dissipation usually contributes terms opposing motion: components proportional to v, v*Abs(v), or sign(v) that remove energy (tend to reduce oscillation amplitude).
- Hardening vs softening behavior often appears as the sign of the cubic stiffness term: -c*x - c*x**3 (hardening) vs -c*x + c*x**3 (softening) leading to amplitude-dependent frequency shifts.
- Limit-cycle/self-excited oscillations are suggested by damping that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v, which injects energy at small amplitude and dissipates at large amplitude.
- External forcing is commonly recognizable as additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms independent of x and v; it can produce resonance and beats.
- Parametric excitation is indicated by multiplicative time dependence on x (or on coefficients of x), e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, leading to Mathieu-type instability regions.
- Dry friction/non-smooth dynamics show up via sign(v) or Abs(v) terms, often producing stick-slip and non-sinusoidal waveforms.
- Coupled nonlinearities like x**2*v or x*v**2 often act as amplitude-dependent damping or frequency modulation terms in normal-form expansions.
- If dv_dt depends weakly or not at all on t, the system is likely autonomous; explicit t-dependence suggests forcing, parameter drift, or nonstationary conditions.

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*Abs(v)**c1 - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed function):
\[
0.415528810853583\sin(t)\;-\;0.0493727442837992\,v^3\;-\;0.291667748408705\,|v|^{1/3}\;-\;1.02930087898757\,x(0.0222734330694684\,t+1)\;-\;1.02930087898757\,x.
\]
So GT contains these essential structures (cannot be removed by choosing constants, because they are present with nonzero coefficients):
- a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (no amplitude/phase freedom in GT beyond what candidate can match),
- a \(v^3\) term,
- an \(|v|^{1/3}\) term (absolute value is essential; domain includes negative \(v\)),
- an \(t x\) term (from \(-1.0293*0.02227\,t x\)),
- an \(x\) term (actually two linear-in-\(x\) contributions combine to \(-2.0586\,x\)).

Thus any matching candidate must be able to represent **both** \(v^3\) and \(|v|^{1/3}\) simultaneously, plus linear \(x\) and \(t x\), plus \(\sin(t)\). None of the candidates include an \(\mathrm{Abs}(v)\) (or equivalent piecewise) operator, so the only hope would be to somehow make a power \(v^{c}\) equal \(|v|^{1/3}\) for all real \(v\), which is impossible in real-valued algebra (for negative \(v\), \(v^{1/3}\) is negative while \(|v|^{1/3}\) is positive). Therefore any candidate lacking an explicit Abs cannot match GT globally.

Now check candidates quickly for any that *do* have Abs (none do) or any other impossible extra terms that cannot be eliminated.

1. Has \(v\), \(\sin(\cdot)\), \(\sin(\cdot v+\cdot)\), \(x\), \(t x\), \(\tanh(\cdot+x)\). No \(v^3\), no \(|v|^{1/3}\). Extra \(\sin(\text{affine in }v)\) and tanh can be zeroed by setting coefficients to 0, but still cannot create both required velocity nonlinearities. No match.

2. Has \(v\), \(\sin(\cdot)\), \(v^{c5}\), \(x\), \(t x\), tanh. Can set \(c5=3\) to get \(v^3\). But cannot produce \(|v|^{1/3}\) (only another single power term exists, and it’s \(v^{c5}\) already used). Also \(v^{1/3}\neq |v|^{1/3}\) globally. No match.

3. Has \(v\), \(v^{c4}\), \(\sin(\cdot)\), plus unwanted \(v^2 x\) and \(t x^3\) (can set their coefficients 0). Still only one power term \(v^{c4}\) besides linear \(v\); cannot represent both \(v^3\) and \(|v|^{1/3}\). No match.

4. Has \(\sin(\cdot t)\), \(\sin(\cdot v)\), \(x\), \(t x\), plus an unavoidable bare \(v\) term (“+ v”) and tanh. The bare \(v\) cannot be removed (coefficient fixed at 1), but GT has no linear \(v\) term. So impossible. No match.

5. Has \(t\), \(v\), \(\sin(\cdot)\), \(x\), \(t x\), tanh. No \(v^3\) nor \(|v|^{1/3}\). No match.

6. Has \(t\), \(v\), \(\sin(\cdot)\), \(\log(c6 x+1)\), constant, \(t x\), tanh. GT has no log/tanh; can zero their coefficients, but still lacks \(v^3\) and \(|v|^{1/3}\). No match.

None include any \(v^3\) or any non-integer/abs velocity power. Even if you set log coefficient 0 and adjust sine phase to \(\sin(t)\) (set frequency 1 and phase 0), the required velocity nonlinearities are missing. No match for 7–16.

17–25. Similar linear \(t,v\), \(\sin(\cdot)\), plus \(\exp(c x)\) or \(\log\), and \(x, t x\). Again no \(v^3\) and no \(|v|^{1/3}\). Exponentials/logs can be zeroed by coefficient choice, but missing required velocity terms. No match for 17–25.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0493727*v³ - 1.02930*(0.02227*t + 1)*x - 1.02930*x + 0.41553*sin(t) - 0.29167*|v|^(1/3)`

Simplifying the GT:
- `0.41553*sin(t)` — sin term
- `-0.0493727*v³` — cubic in v
- `-0.29167*|v|^(1/3)` — cube root of |v|
- `-1.02930*(0.02227*t + 1)*x - 1.02930*x = -1.02930*0.02227*t*x - 1.02930*x - 1.02930*x = -0.02293*t*x - 2.05860*x`

So GT = `0.41553*sin(t) - 0.0493727*v³ - 0.29167*|v|^(1/3) - 2.05860*x - 0.02293*t*x`

The key basis functions in GT are:
1. `sin(t)` 
2. `v³`
3. `|v|^(1/3)`
4. `x`
5. `t*x`

No `t` standalone term, no constant term, no `tanh`, no `log`, no `exp`.

Now I need to check each candidate for whether it can reproduce these exact basis functions. The critical issue is that GT contains `v³` and `|v|^(1/3)` — these are nonlinear functions of v that cannot be represented by linear combinations of other basis functions.

Let me check candidates that have `v**c` terms (which could represent v³ or |v|^(1/3)):

**Candidates 2, 3, 43, 44, 45:** These have `v**c` terms but only ONE such term. GT needs TWO nonlinear v terms (v³ and |v|^(1/3)), so a single `v**c` cannot match both.

**Candidates with sin(v):** Candidates 1, 4 have `sin(v)` terms — sin(v) ≠ v³ or |v|^(1/3).

**Candidates with exp(v):** 26, 35, 41, 46, 47, 48, 49, 50 — exp(v) cannot represent v³ or |v|^(1/3).

**Candidates with only linear v:** Most remaining candidates (5-42 excluding those above) have only `c*v` (linear in v). Linear v cannot represent v³ or |v|^(1/3).

**Candidates with tanh, log, exp of x:** These add basis functions not in GT, but more importantly, they still lack the v³ and |v|^(1/3) terms.

Let me verify systematically — every candidate needs BOTH v³ and |v|^(1/3) terms. No candidate has both. The candidates with `v**c` (2, 3, 43, 44, 45) have only one power-law term in v, which can match at most one of {v³, |v|^(1/3)}.

Since v³ and |v|^(1/3) are linearly independent basis functions, and no candidate contains both, none can match.
